### Post by Masoris on 2008-08-05
LaRoza could be a Esperanto name. "La" means "the", and "Roz" means "rose".
Generally Esperanto speakers prefer to use suffix "-o" for male, and "-a" for female. So "LaRozo" is male name, and "LaRoza" is female name.

I was hypothesizing that LaRoza may be transsexual or a hermaphrodite; also noting that she'd rather be known for her technical knowledge than something biological about her.  "LaRoza: a knowledgeable computer user" sounds better than "LaRoza: a knowledgeable, transsexual computer user."  It's kind of a slap in the face to work so hard in an area of study only to have some biological trait have an equal standing in your identity compared to all that you have worked for.

Yes, yes, I know there is more to someone's identity than can be summed up in a single sentence, but if you had to summarize yourself in a short sentence, like the title that appears below someones name on a TV interview, what would you want your title to say?  It would be a double standard, as no one bothers to specify someone as straight or having brown hair.

I wouldn't know.

I never said that imagination is useless. I was simply trying to point out that imagination should be a counterpart to action. The mind was paired with the body for a reason. I love imagination. Being one of few I've met able to accomplish the feat of imagination, I find it invaluable. But if you sit there and imagine what you *could* do all day, you lose that day. I too, had nothing (except a mother who taught me that "Why?" should never be answered with "Because I said so."). Now, when I decide I'd like to have something, I start making steps towards obtaining it. I also find that interaction with other members of the human race (while not enlightening) is a good exercise in problem-solving. Anyway, about the age of this boy... it's insignificant, as far as I'm concerned, I left it blank on purpose. The sex comment was related to my preferences, rather than his experiences.
(Although I would suggest it. It's quite invigorating, and very few dislike it. (While you may turn out to be one of these few, it's generally more fun to try things than decide they can't be any fun, and it gives better stories.))

EDIT: TO CLARIFY: I WAS NOT ADVOCATING THE KILLING OF THE MIND. I WAS SAYING THAT IMAGINATION ALONE SHOULDN'T COMPLETELY COMPOSE A LIFE. EXPERIENCES WILL NOT ONLY SUPPLEMENT A LIFE FULL OF IMAGINATION NICELY, BUT WILL ALSO ENRICH THE IMAGINATION, PROVIDING NEW MATERIAL FOR THE EXERCISE OF IT.

### Post by lukjad on 2008-08-11
The only time that you may use the term "can not" is when the "can" is split from the word "not" to designate that you are able to abstain from some action at which point the word "not" carries the emphasis.

For example: 

You can not go to the party.

Means:

You can choose to not go to the party.

I stand corrected. Thank you, LaRoza, for your timely intervention. :)

---

### Post by Canis familiaris on 2008-08-11
can't?

---

### Post by lukjad on 2008-08-11
"Can't" is always an abreviation of "cannot" because it denotes the inability, rather than the possibility of not doing something. (I think.)

---

### Post by lukjad on 2008-08-11
True. "Can" means able to while "May" means permission.

"Can I lift this desk?" This is asking if you have the physical ability to lift the mass of that desk.

"May I have a cookie?" This is asking for permission (from your Mom) to have a sweet snack just before dinner.

LAROZA(1)									LAROZA(1)

NAME

       LaRoza - A light for dark times

SYNOPSIS

       LaRoza [options] [file ..]
       LaRoza [options] -
       LaRoza [options] -t tag
       LaRoza [options] -q [errorfile]

       ex
       view
       gLaRoza gview eLaRoza eview
       rLaRoza rview rgLaRoza rgview

DESCRIPTION

       LaRoza 
OPTIONS

       The options may be given in  any  order,  before  or  after  requests.
       Options without an argument can be combined after a single dash.

       -h       {help} send out a distress call to LaRoza.
       -s       {save} Not to be confused with the s option, you save the
conversation for further pondering.
       -sh      {save and help} Very much different than the -s and -h 
options, this options calls for a regulation of a dispute. Unfortunately, 
the person who calls may very well end with the short end of the stick. 
Use with caution
       -e       {enter} This is an invitation for LaRoza to enter into
the thread and post comments. 
       -x       {surrender} This is not so much a command but a comment.
If you find yourself arguing against LaRoza and loosing (that is to say,
always), adding this option will signal that you have conceded the point
and now acknowledge that you were wrong at all the time.
       -l       {leave} The leave function is one of the more useful and
dangerous options you can find. It, combined with the following commands
...
Time Up. Please re-login:

### Post by Canis familiaris on 2008-09-11
> **LaRoza said:**
> (Hmm... When I quote this, the maatraa "i" in "kiya" is moved one place over (which is impossible, as another maatraa follows that...)
???

> Since I am learning and haven't achieved perfection yet, was I correct? (Except my weird transliteration of "khusi", no special symbols here and I am used to IAST)
kushi should has been spelt as khushi I think. AFAIK English has no pronounciation for &#2326;. We use kh for transliterate.

> And, you said "apne bhi mujhe bahut khushi kiya". I haven't quite gotten the hang of apne, is it referring to you or me? "oneself also me to much happiness done".
Is that the same as "you and me both"? (I know mujhko == mujhe)

It's aapne. I think you are confusing it with apne.(&#2310;&#2346;&#2344;&#2375; != &#2309;&#2346;&#2344;&#2375;). &#2310;&#2346;&#2344;&#2375;(aapne) means &#2310;&#2346; &#2344;&#2375; i.e. you have (in my sentence you have also made me very happy). &#2309;&#2346;&#2344;&#2375;(apne) is oneself and also a noun refering to near and dear ones.
Also I meant khush not khushi. If I meant khushi the sentence would have been: You have also made me very happiness, which would make no sense.
Also use mujhe instead of mujhko. I am not sure Why but I remember learning the same some time ago.

### Post by gunashekar on 2008-09-11
> **LaRoza said:**
> 

What does &#2344;&#2375; mean?




&#2344;&#2375; (Nay or Ne) is a suffix to indicate "have/has done... )
Like
Aap   tum or tuu is "you" and aapne tumne tuune used in a sentence means " you have...."
Hum-ne -- I have....
Us-ne  - He/She/It has ....
Duniya-ne - The world has....

---

### Post by LaRoza on 2008-09-11
> **gunashekar said:**
> &#2344;&#2375; (Nay or Ne) is a suffix to indicate "have/has done... )
Like
Aap   tum or tuu is "you" and aapne tumne tuune used in a sentence means " you have...."
Hum-ne -- I have....
Us-ne  - He/She/It has ....
Duniya-ne - The world has....

Thanks. Is it a postposition? Does its "subject" have to be in the oblique case (it seems so)?

### Post by LaRoza on 2008-09-13
> **lukjad007 said:**
> Thou doth knowest mine heart, lad.

Wrong.

"Thou dost" is just the first correction.

That isn't middle English, it is modern English with archaic pronouns. The grammar is the same, just the three pronouns "thou", "thee", "ye" are not used.

thou == Second person singular familiar
thee == Second person plural familiar
ye == Second person singular formal
you == Second person plural formal

---

### Post by Faolan84 on 2008-09-13
Ah, another admirer of the English language and it's archaic forms?

Actually, to make things more complicated the plural forms are also the dynamic forms. It's more correct to address royalty or holy folk as you and ye and not thou and thee. plus to make things even worse there is the whole case issue with Middle English were some nouns have subjective, genitive, and dative cases. It makes my head spin sometimes, but I can read Chaucer fluently.

---

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-09-14
> **LaRoza said:**
> Wrong.

"Thou dost" is just the first correction.

That isn't middle English, it is modern English with archaic pronouns. The grammar is the same, just the three pronouns "thou", "thee", "ye" are not used.

thou == Second person singular familiar
thee == Second person plural familiar
ye == Second person singular formal
you == Second person plural formal

I only read the few posts, but I just learned more about middle English than I ever cared to know. One thing that bugged me, though, was how God was often referred to with the familiar form (in the KJV)... For those irked like me, you might find this interesting:

"As William Tyndale translated the Bible into English in the early 1500s, he sought to preserve the singular and plural distinctions that he found in his Hebrew and Greek originals. Therefore, he consistently used thou for the singular and ye for the plural regardless of the relative status of the speaker and the addressee. By doing so, he probably saved thou from utter obscurity and gave it an air of solemnity that sharply distinguished it from its French counterpart. Tyndale's usage was imitated in the King James Bible, and remained familiar because of that translation." ~wikipedia

I honestly (given the nature of most of the posts here) never figured I'd learn anything even remotely useful from this thread.:lolflag:

### Post by Faolan84 on 2008-09-15

---

### Post by LaRoza on 2008-09-16
> **Faolan Devyn Aodfin said:**
> 
From what I see on Softpedia sysres is like System Restore in Windows XP. Interesting. I didn't think there was anything like that for Linux.

The softpedia people added it themselves (I had nothing to do with that).

The goal of sysres is to be like Windows's System Restore, because of the people asking for it on this forum (do a search for it, you'll see many threads requesting it.)

This is the first one I could find that does this. I have seen other backup programs, but none like this one.

It is much better than Windows system restore. Because Linux lacks a registery, it doesn't have the criticality of Windows and it is takes up much less space (a matter of kilobytes (about 4) for several restore points).

It also works much faster and is much more flexible. It has a GTK and QT interface (and when started, will use the one it can) and a command line interface and a command line argument interface (which I use, and wrote for myself)

---

Angrezi ki tarah Hindi ki shuddh prayog bahut hota hai. Hindi me~ Urdu, angrezi, karasi, aur kuch aur bhasha ke shubdai~ ka prayog hota hai~. Uske ilaya alag pradesho me~ bhi alag dang se Hindi boli jati hai.
I'll give the transliteration:
Angrezi ki tarah Hindi ka shuddh prayog kam hota hain. Hindi mein Urdu, Angrezi, Farsi aur kuch aur bhasha ke shadbo ka prayog hota hai, iske ilava alag pradesho mein alag dhang se hindi boli jati hain.

Which means:
Like English, Hindi is not often used in pure form. In Hindi there are Urdu, English, and Persian Words used. Furthermore, in different states Hindi is spoken in different manner.

Wikipedia
Spontaneous recovery helps explain why it is so hard to overcome drug addictions. For example, cocaine addicts who are thought to be "cured" can experience an irresistible impulse to use the drug again if they are subsequently confronted by a stimulus with strong connections to the drug, such as a white powder (O'Brien et al., 1992; Drummond et al., 1995; DiCano & Everitt, 2002). Wikapedia

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-10-27
On the note of ninjas... I'm pretty sure that the human eye notices motion, then silhouette, then color. If you're going to silhouette yourself against the sky you should make sure that you don't look like a human... and if you don't want to attract attention it's also important that you not move.

Basically, you don't want to silhouette yourself against any light source, it'll get you noticed way before they see that your ninja-clothes clash with your ninja shoes.

Pirates on the other hand... :lolflag:

### Post by jdong on 2008-11-11
This is the official statement from the Forum Council regarding the matter:

> 
There was recently a staff account compromised by another forum member, LaRoza. As a result, this individual is no longer welcome at the forums community.

Here at UbuntuForums we take security very seriously, and would like to remind everyone to do the same in safeguarding their access credentials. Remember that unauthorized access to others' accounts, whether or not in a manner you consider white-hat or harmless, is against the spirit of Ubuntu outlined in the Code of Conduct and will result in the appropriate consequences.

The Forum Council


With that said, I don't think it's fair or appropriate to discuss the circumstances while the affected individual is not allowed to participate. I suggest we move on to other topics of discussion.
